2.  Contract or Task Order Title.  LHC Support Services II.

3.  Background.  As a subordinate unit to Headquarters, Air Force Space Command, 24th Air Force, and the 688th Information Operations Wing, the
38th Cyberspace Readiness Squadron, LHC Flight (38 CYRS/SCC) executes Air Force Space Commands Defense Information Systems Network (DISN) Lead
Command responsibilities, which include DISN services requirements, provisioning, programming, funding and management, consolidated Major
Command (MAJCOM) Circuit Management Office (MAJCOM CMO), Mobile Satellite Services (MSS) and Air Force/Department of Defense (DoD) Teleport
services.  38 CYRS/SCC supports all Air Force units, as well as DOD and Federal service and agency tenants on Air Force installations worldwide
that require interbase DISN connectivity and/or associated services.  The MAJCOM CMO provides the consolidated MAJCOM-level circuit management
office functions and customer support to field units of all 11 Air Force MAJCOMs.  Reflecting the evolving nature of the Air Force environment
of technology, policy, and resources, the MAJCOM CMO may be soon providing similar support for Forward Operating Agencies (FOAs) and Direct
Reporting Units (DRUs), as well as adding Fixed Satellite Services (FSS) to its group of satellite support services.  The SCC Flight is
responsible for the overall programming and management of AF corporate LHC program funding, as well as individual MAJCOM execution year funds
for MAJCOM-unique circuit requirements and services. In addition to coordination with DISA and DITCO to provide required DISN services, 38
CYRS/SCC also leverages other support contracts, such as the GSA NETWORX and DISA-GSA Future Commercial Satellite Acquisition (FCSA), to meet
Air Force mission requirements.  Personnel of the 38 CYRS/SCC interface with all levels of the AF and other DoD and Federal Services and
Agencies to accomplish the Flights assigned missions.  Further, 38 CYRS/SCC has overseen development, sustainment and support of software tools
such as the Telecommunications Certification Office Support System (TCOSS) and Facility Circuit Inventory Tracking (FaCIT) which have assisted
the Air Forces corporate and base-level DISN circuit management and funding activities.  Again reflecting the evolving Air Force environment,
these software tools are being reexamined for their continuing value and available funding.

4.  Objectives:  The purpose of this contract is to support the 38 CYRS/SCC LHC Flight in their mission execution of DISN Enterprise services
provisioning, programming, funding, policy and management.  This contract provides DISN and telecommunications circuit and services provisioning
subject matter and technical expertise to develop, program, manage and execute the Air Forces DISN Lead Command and Common-User DISN
requirements management responsibilities.  This contract provides provisioning and communications technical support to enable the Department of
the Air Force to provide telecommunications services, circuit support and management services for their Air Force, DOD, and Federal customers.
This contract provides communications provisioning, policy and technical support for the Air Force DISN Lead Command, MAJCOMs, field units, and
tenants.  This contract also provides software, system, and network development, sustainment, operations, security and customer support for the
TCOSS and FaCIT systems, following standards of DoD, AF, and applicable industry and ADP best practices in administration, software development,
and Information Assurance. This contract provides MSS and Teleport planning, programming, technical support, management, policy, and customer
support. All work will be performed in accordance  with applicable DOD, Service, and DISA regulations, instructions, directives, technical
orders, guidance, and law, and as directed by the COR or ACOR.  Contractor staff will assist Government (38 CYRS/SCC) staff in completing
relevant DISN LHC tasks levied on the office from time to time as are relevant to LHC mission oversight and the purposes of this contract.  This
contract also includes optional provisions reflecting the evolving AF and DoD environment of satellite, circuit provisioning, and funding: to
expand the MSS task scope to include fixed commercial satellite systems in anticipation of the Flight assigned this additional mission by the
Air Force; to optionally expand the CMO to support AF FOAs and DRUs; to support further development of TCOSS (separate from sustainment
activities); and to support continuing FaCIT development, sustainment, and customer support.

5.  Scope.  In support of the 38 CYRS, the Contractor shall provide trained and experienced technicians with the ability to develop, operate,
maintain, and enhance the existing capabilities of the AF communications long haul infrastructure.  This support includes using information and
communications technology professional services for the DISN LHC Lead Command support, Air Force Common User and MAJCOM CMO functions, TCOSS,
FaCIT, MSS, Air Force customers of DISA-mandated commercial telecommunications contracts, and Air Force/Department of Defense (AF/DoD) Teleport
services.  Contractor shall support these programs and associated applications essential to enable the Air Force to provide telecommunications
acquisition and management services for their use and use by their respective service management functions, DISA, and other DoD customers.
Contractor personnel shall provide customer support for internal and external LHC and CMO customers.  Customer support includes DISN LHC
software applications support for TCOSS, FACIT, and associated DISN business systems.  Specific areas of expertise shall include database
management, web development, client server technologies, information assurance, network security, and process management.  Contractor personnel
shall recommend, comply with, and document a structured software development process that includes requirements gathering and analysis, design,
development, documentation, testing, release, and best practices.  Contractor personnel shall transition and/or support the software
applications migration to Web environments using Microsoft SQL, .NET, and IIS products, or other software technologies as specified.  Contractor
personnel shall support system interfaces with the DISA and other organizations as specified.  Contractor personnel shall obtain and maintain
any Network and Security certifications required to support the applications.  The Program Manager (PM), in conjunction with the Configuration
Control Board (CCB)s Army, Air Force, Navy and DISA representatives, provides overall direction of the system and its applications.  Contractor
personnel shall assist in all financial management processes necessary for LHC financial planning and budget execution and reporting.
Contractor personnel shall execute Air Force and MAJCOM CMO functions, including support for acquisition, provisioning, message routing and
tracking, Communications Service Authorizations (CSA), expiring and expired CSAs, and Review and Revalidations (R&R).  CMO functions shall
include expanded support hours for coverage based upon time zones.  The Contractor will support AF efforts to identify and realize DISN LHC
efficiencies.  Contractor personnel may be required to attend meetings outside the Scott Air Force Base (AFB) commuting area.  Contractor
personnel shall, under contract options, continue to develop the systems with expanded functionality for program managers, financial and
provisioning communities, and base level users.  Contractor personnel shall, under contract options, continue to enhance integration
functionality to provide greater integration with other DISA provisioning automation systems.   Contractor personnel shall, under the TCOSS
Development contract option, continue to develop the system with such desired enhancements for program managers, financial and provisioning
communities, and base level users, as proposed by interested users and directed by the Program Manager.  Contractor personnel shall, under the
Commercial Satellite Management Office (CSMO) contract option, perform the combined functions of the existing MSS and Teleport functions with
Fixed Satellite System (FSS) functions for Air Force satellite system usage management.  Contractor personnel shall, under the FaCIT
Development, Sustainment, and Customer Support option, sustain, further develop, manage, test, and secure the FaCIT system in the development
environment provided, and support its customers.  Contractor personnel shall, under the Air Force Forward Operating Agencies (FOAs) and Direct
Supporting Units (DRUs), support such units as part of the MAJCOM CMO with all tasks appropriate to that office.  If a given option is
exercised, all contractor team members assigned to that option are required to also perform tasks identified as common to all team members, some
examples being performing travel, writing and updating continuity documents, and providing regular reports of activities

6.  Specific Tasks.
Required ranges for Full Time Equivalent (FTE) personnel counts are shown for many tasks.  The contractor shall propose a suitable number of
personnel within those ranges to perform a given task.

6.1  Task 1 - Contract Administration Support.  Tasks common to all areas of the contract are listed here for clarity.  All contractor team
members shall contribute to the completion of these tasks.

6.1.1  Subtask 1 - Provide Project Management Plan.  The contractor shall provide a  Project Management Plan (PMP).  The PMP reports the methods
and approach for the technical and functional activities required for completing the tasks required by this SOW.  The PMP shall include
estimated completion dates with proposed milestones for completing all major task established in this SOW.  Quality assurance, progress/status
reporting and program reviews are also required. It is prepared at the start of the contract and is updated at the beginning of each option
year.  Format shall conform to Data Item Description (DID) DI-MGMT-80004A, as tailored by Contract Data Requirements List (CDRL) A001.

Deliverable: Project Management Plan

6.1.2  Subtask 2 - Orientation meeting to government contract staff.  The Contractor shall meet with the Government staff for the contract
within five (5) working days of contract award.  The purpose of this meeting is for primary personnel of both Contractor and Government to
become acquainted with staff contacts of the contract and expected interactions.  The meeting will be at Government offices or another pre-
agreed location nearby.  Minutes shall be provided within two working days following meeting.  Minutes shall be composed in Microsoft Office
Word or a compatible electronic file format, structured in Contractor-determined layout, and emailed to the COR, and copy to Government Program
Manager at addresses provided.

Deliverable: Minutes of Orientation Meeting

6.1.3 Subtask 3 Provide reports of activities.

6.1.3.1  Subtask 3.1  Provide monthly report.  The Contractor shall provide a periodic report of activities as a Monthly Status Report, using
text and charts in describing staff activities, accomplishments, TCOSS and FaCIT system operations, Circuit Management  activities, in
accordance with deliverable description in paragraph 11.

Deliverable:     Monthly Status Report

6.1.3.2  Subtask 3.2  Provide weekly report.  The Contractor shall provide a weekly activity report (WAR) briefly summarizing important
activities and accomplishments during the week past, each activity in no more than a paragraph in Government format.  Due date and time of this
weekly report may be adjusted from time to time.

Deliverable:     WAR Report

6.1.4  Subtask 4  Hold regular meetings with COR.  The contractor shall hold regular monthly meetings  with the Government COR and ACOR to
discuss items of concern to the Contractor and the Government about the execution and administration of the contract.  Possible other attendees
include other Contractor representatives and Government representatives.  These are not Program Management Reviews and attendee count should be
limited.  Expect meetings to usually last an hour.  Site will usually be Government offices.

Deliverable:     Meeting Minutes

6.1.5  Subtask 5 - Feedback on systems and processes.  For all tasks and subtasks within the scope of this contract, the contractor shall
provide suggestions on improvement of systems and business processes, to COR and ACOR.  Examples include the DISA Direct Order Entry (DDOE)
system, TCOSS, and DISAs R&R process.

Deliverable:     Documented issues and suggested solutions

6.1.6 Subtask 6 - Review draft, new, existing or updated DoD, CJCS, and DISA directives and instructions.  Using expertise, knowledge, and
research, the contractor shall assess and determine how proposed changes will affect AF LHC policy and governance.  Provide in assigned format
at or before desired time due to the COR and ACOR.

Deliverable:     Provide findings on how changes will impact AF LHC policy

6.1.7 Subtask 7 - Provide input to AF policy and governance.  The contractor shall assist AF representatives in determining the long-haul
provisioning process and long-haul management policy.

6.1.8 Subtask 8  Advise on impact of  policies on LHC tools.  The contractor shall advise the PM on Air Force, DISA, and DoD policies affecting
TCOSS, FaCIT (if option is exercised), and web software, and the supporting software packages.

6.1.9 Subtask 9  Support data research for systems.  The contractor shall perform supporting data research using AF and DISA/DITCO data support
systems.  These include (but are not limited to) systems such as TCOSS, Cyberspace Infrastructure Planning System (CIPS), Telecommunications
Inventory and Billing Information (TIBI) system, and World-Wide  Online Systems (WWOLS).

6.1.10 Subtask 10  Support within-scope LHC ad hoc tasks.  Due to the nature of 38 CYRS/SCCs DISN LHC mission, the contractor shall provide
Subject Matter Expert (SME) support in accomplishment of these higher-headquarters tasks.  Tasks include, but are not limited to, DISN and LHC
related briefings, papers, studies and reports.  Type of  responses may be (but not limited to): email,  briefings, information papers, reports,
and metrics.

6.1.11 Subtask 11  Manage, track, and care for Government Furnished Equipment (GFE).  GFE shall be tracked by a Contractor-appointed Equipment
Custodian.  GFE software and hardware appears in the provided GFE List (see paragraph 13).  Quarterly the Contractor shall provide a list of
broken items, of hardware and software updates required for the contract, of software licenses, and of updates performed for various purposes
(such as security, software tool updates) in accordance with DoD, Air Force, and DISA directives and guidance, as well as Air Force and Base
network oversight personnel directives and guidance.  Contractor Equipment Custodian shall cooperate with and assist the appointed Government
Custodians in tracking equipment and software provided under the contract.  This task does not authorize any funds expenditures by the
Contractor.

Deliverable:     List of repair items
            List of required updates (anticipated and performed)

6.2 Task 2  Circuit management activities.  Circuit management activities are common to both the AF Major Command Circuit Management Office
(Task 3) and the AF Enterprise Long Haul Management Office (Task 4).   The contractor shall perform telecommunications circuit management and
provisioning activities in support of AF Major Commands and their subordinate units, DoD and Federal organization/agency tenants on Air Force
installations.  No DoD 8570.01-M certification is required for these tasks.  All contractor team members performing Tasks 3 and 4 shall also
perform these tasks.

6.2.1 Subtask 1  Perform in accordance with official guidance.  The contractor shall perform all circuit and service provisioning functions in
accordance with DoD Directives and Instructions, CJCS Directives and Instructions, DISA Circulars and Provisioning Notices, DITCO Instructions,
AF Instructions and Manuals, LHC/MAJCOM Service Level Agreements (SLA), and guidance from AF subject matter experts.

6.2.2 Subtask 2 - Validate/accept/reject circuit or service provisioning orders.  In accordance with Air Force guidance, the contractor shall
ensure provisioning orders in DDOE are accurate and contain all the required documentation, and comply with official guidance before the orders
are approved.  Approve validated orders in DDOE.  Deny, with coordination with the customer and COR, all orders that do not contain the required
documentation and return to the customer for correction.

Deliverables:    Monthly status report

6.2.3 Subtask 3  Create circuit orders.  The contractor shall create circuit orders in DDOE.  Most orders will be created by the customer, DISA
personnel, or the Air Force Systems Networking (AFSN) office (AFMC Electronic Systems Center/HIZB, Maxwell AFB-Gunter Annex, Montgomery AL,
email  HIZB.AFSN@Gunter.af.mil).

6.2.4 Subtask 4  Expired and expiring Communication Service Authorization (CSA) (Expired CSA) program.  The contractor shall manage,
coordinate, and execute the Expired CSA program for AF Program Designator Codes (PDCs).  Review CSA tracking in TCOSS to ensure units are
accomplishing re-award of expired and expiring CSAs that still have a bona fide need, and ensure units are discontinuing CSAs no longer needed.
Contractor will ensure re-award actions are completed in advance of CSA expiration and will ensure timely discontinue actions to ensure payment
for unneeded services are kept to a minimum.

Deliverables:    Monthly status report

6.2.5 Subtask 5  Assist with LHC issues.  The contractor shall provide assistance to AF LHC customers including, but not limited to, MAJCOMs,
their subordinate units, Combatant Commands, and AF base tenants on LHC related issues including the preparation of DDOE circuit and service
Telecommunications Request (TR) orders, technical and policy guidance, billing issues, and Networx services.

6.2.6 Subtask 6 - Perform circuit and CSA discrepancy reviews.  The contractor shall identify LHC circuits and CSAs that are no longer being
utilized. In coordination with the customer, develop and successfully execute discontinue orders for those circuits to minimize costs and
recapture funds.

6.2.7 Subtask 7 - Transition communications circuits/services from expiring contracts to new contracts.  The contractor shall coordinate with 38
CYRS/SCC, DISA/DITCO, GSA, MAJCOMs, vendors, and customers to successfully transition circuits/services from expiring contracts to new
contracts.

Deliverables:    Monthly status report

6.2.8 Subtask 8 - Provide circuit requirement design and technical review.  The contractor shall review customer requirements and DISA solutions
to ensure proper circuit design and engineering to accommodate the customers needs.  Make recommendations and provide alternatives to
customers.  Work with 38 CYRS/SCC, DISA, DITCO and the customer to ensure customer needs are met.

6.2.9 Subtask 9 - Coordinate and track circuit actions.  The contractor shall coordinate and provide assistance to customers requesting circuits
and/or services, throughout the provisioning lifecycle.  Provide coordination between the base, vendor, and DISA; and ensure customers are
satisfied with new service.  Document all circuit actions, using TCOSS.

6.2.10 Subtask 10 - Assist circuit improvement.  Working with the Air Force DISN Lead Command, representatives of AF Major Commands, their
subordinate units, Combatant Commands, DOD/Federal agency tenants, and DISA, the contractor shall recommend changes to long haul circuits and
services to improve operational capability, economic viability, and the meeting of mission needs.

Deliverable:  Monthly status report

6.3 Task 3 - MAJCOM Consolidated Circuit Management Office (CMO).  The contractor shall perform Circuit Management Office activities in support
of AF Major Commands, their subordinate units, and Combatant Commands on AF bases.  No DoD 8570.01-M certification is required for these tasks.
The authorized allotted FTE range count for this task is nine to fourteen (9-14).

6.3.1 Subtask 1 - Review and Revalidation (R&R) program.  The contractor shall manage and coordinate the R&R program activities in support of AF
Major Commands, their subordinate units, and Combatant Commands on AF bases.  Review DISAs R&R database daily to ensure units are accomplishing
R&R of circuits under their purview.  All circuits must have R&R completed no later than every 2 years IAW AF and DOD policy.

Deliverables:    R&R Monthly Status

6.3.2 Subtask 2 - Establish/maintain DDOE routing matrices and Central Address Directory (CAD).  The contractor shall add and remove personnel
from the routing matrices and ensure the routing matrix reflects accurate routing tables for the AF enterprise.  Ensure the CAD has up-to-date
Points of Contact (POC) information and remove POCs when they no longer require access to DDOE.  Upon receipt of a change request, complete
updates within 2 duty days from notification.

Deliverable:     Updated matrix, CAD table

6.3.3 Subtask 3 - Manage/approve DDOE Roles.  The contractor shall manage/approve DDOE roles within the respective MAJCOMs in accordance with
DOD and AF instructions and policy.

6.3.4 Subtask 4 - Manage inter-command transfer of circuit inventory.  The contractor and MAJCOM CMO personnel shall work together to identify
circuits and/or services for transfer between Commands.

Deliverable: Completed associated orders and tasks to transfer circuits/services.

6.4 Task 4  AF Enterprise Long Haul Management Office.  The contractor shall perform AF wide circuit and service management and analysis
activities in support of the LHC Requirements Lead and enterprise AF policy.  No DoD 8570.01-M certification is required for these tasks.  The
authorized allotted FTE range count for this task is five to six (5-6).

6.4.1 Subtask 1  Analysis for Enterprise LHC.  The contractor shall provide query, analysis, metrics, trending and reporting in support of AF
Enterprise LHC Management, DISN Subscription Services (DSS), and AF Telecommunication activities to the COR.  Work with appropriate
Service/Agency, AF MAJCOM, AF Base, AF Tenant, and/or DISA/DITCO representatives to rectify and correct discrepancies and drive AF efficiencies.

6.4.2 Subtask 2  Assist requirements determination.  The contractor shall assist in the determination of AF DISN telecommunication dedicated
and common user requirements and resource impacts.  Communicate with all AF customers on their requirements and issues.

6.4.3 Subtask 3  Perform impact assessment.  The contractor shall perform analysis and impact assessments on the DISN and resources based on
existing requirements, DISA programs, transitions and projected changes in technologies.

6.4.4 Subtask 4  Query and analyze circuit records.  The contractor shall perform query, data extraction and analysis of AF wide circuit
inventory in 38 CYRS/SCC databases.

6.4.5 Subtask 5  Query, analyze DoD circuit inventory list.  The contractor shall analyze DoD wide circuit inventory lists from DISA databases
for service type and provide bandwidth threshold reports based on the current DISN Subscription Services Matrix chart.  Maintain currency and
accuracy of inventory binders for organizational daily access. Use Microsoft Excel spreadsheets, including functions, macros, Visual Basic for
Application routines, to validate, process and manage database extracts to ensure accuracy and completeness based on DISN services and actual
provisioned bandwidth. Data exists on classified and must be scrubbed for unclassified use prior to placing in binders in an unclassified
environment.

Deliverable:     Inventory listings
            Scripts

6.4.6 Subtask 6  Analyze and substantiate telecommunication issues.  The contractor shall analyze and substantiate telecommunication issues by
review of variety of AF and DISA/DITCO provided provisioning documentation to drive AF efficiencies.  These may be (but not limited to) Delayed
Service Reports (DSRs), Status of Acquisition Message (SAM), and Ready For Use (RFU) records.  Ensure proper Program Designator Code (PDC) used
for DISN requirements.  Work with appropriate AF financial manager and/or DISA/DITCO organization to remedy inconsistencies.

6.4.7 Subtask 7  Perform AF Enterprise-wide DISN transition activities.  The contractor shall perform AF Enterprise wide DISN telecommunication
transition related activities in support of, and guided by, the COR.

6.4.8 Subtask 8  Perform data research support.  The contractor shall perform LHC telecommunications data research support using AF,
DISA/DITCO, and vendor managed data support systems.  These include (but are not limited to) TCOSS, TIBI, CIPS.

6.4.9 Subtask 9  Provide SME advice.  The contractor shall provide recommendations to the COR/ACOR orally and in writing in response to taskers
and downward directed reporting requirements.

6.4.10 Subtask 10  Provide COR/ACOR current information.  The contractor shall provide the COR/ACOR current information on Information
Technology (IT) and Services derived from briefings, telephone conferences, web/printed articles, magazine, news organizations, and other
definitive sources  about AF programs, projects and system implementation that may impact DISN bandwidth, services, and policy.

6.4.11 Subtask 11 - AF Enterprise Site Support Contract.  The contractor shall provide analysis of DISA technical solutions to the COR/ACOR and
AF customers and assist issue resolution regarding the DISN LHC site support (Last Half Mile) contract  Site Support provides connectivity
between a DISN circuit and a base delivery point.  Contractors may need to interact with personnel of DISA/DITCO, the Air Force and other
Services/Agencies, and vendors.  Escalate unresolved issues to COR/ACOR.

Deliverable:     Verbal and written communications of task progress
Analysis of Site Support monthly report with status update on circuit actions

6.4.12 Subtask 12 - Networx Transition and Customer Support.  The contractor shall assist AF personnel with analysis and document preparation in
support of AF Designated Agency Representative (DAR) Administrator (DAR Admin) for the General Services Administration (GSA) Networx contract.
May require access to vendor secure Web portals.  Report on task characteristics and outstanding points.

Deliverable:     Verbal and written communications of task progress

6.4.12.1 The contractor shall assist identification and validation of existing circuit inventory.

6.4.12.2 The contractor shall coordinate with customers, MAJCOM and subordinate units, DITCO, GSA, and Networx Vendors to resolve inventory and
billing issues, and to assist DAR Admin in maintaining point-of-contact information.

6.4.12.3 The contractor shall assist AF users with Networx administrative matters.

6.4.12.4 The contractor shall assist in the resolution of specific transition issues related to Networx (and follow-on contract).

6.5 Task 5 - TCOSS Maintenance, Security, and Customer Support.  The contractor shall perform all software, hardware, network, security, and
customer support functions for TCOSS. Changes will be done after submission to CCB and approval by PM in Configuration Control Board (CCB).  All
tasks must comply with DoD, Joint, AF, DISA, MAJCOM, and Scott AFB standards for interoperability, software lifecycle, security, and customer
support Directives, Instructions, Memoranda, and other official guidance.  The authorized allotted FTE range count for this task is four to five
(4-5).

6.5.1  Subtask 1 - Systems Maintenance.  The contractor shall maintain TCOSS software code, structure, and functions.  General programming,
analysis, and design tasks require no DoD 8570.01-M certification.  Code repository and system administrative responsibilities (examples include
backup, replication, security, migration to production) require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level
II, being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

Deliverable:     Application code

6.5.1.1 The contractor shall maintain the common web oriented application framework for TCOSS.

6.5.1.2 The contractor shall utilize Object Oriented analysis, design and development methodologies and techniques.

6.5.1.3 The contractor shall provide development in Microsoft Visual Studio with VB.NET, ASP.NET, and JavaScript languages.

6.5.1.4 The contractor shall use the Microsoft Visual Studio team development support to manage the software development life cycle.

6.5.1.5 The contractor shall ensure TCOSS functions, procedures and data interfaces in TCOSS reflect the changing role of DISA support elements
within the long-haul provisioning process.

6.5.1.6 The contractor shall use IEEE 12207 (3 volumes), ITIL (Information Technology Infrastructure Library), and similar DoD standards for
Configuration Management, Change Management, and Release Management processes to plan, identify, control, monitor, verify, and manage software
configuration items.

6.5.1.6 The contractor shall record and report information needed to effectively manage established baselines and those being established during
the development process.

6.5.1.7 The contractor shall ensure all code is Year 2000 compliant.

6.5.2 Subtask 2 - Web Site Support.  The contractor shall maintain Web site software code, data, structure and functions.  General programming,
analysis, and design tasks require no DoD 8570.01-M certification.  Code repository and system administrative responsibilities (examples include
backup, replication, security, migration to production) require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level
II, being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

6.5.2.1 The contractor shall manage site architecture and configuration.

6.5.2.2 The contractor shall maintain static and dynamically data generated web based client user interfaces.

6.5.2.3 The contractor shall manage site security and policies.

6.5.2.4 The contractor shall collect and monitor site performance and usage statistics and provide analysis report.

Deliverable:           Statistics and analysis report

6.5.2.5 The contractor shall ensure that site design standards adhere to Section 508 guidelines.  Section 508 requires that federal agencies
electronic and information technology is accessible to people with disabilities.

6.5.3  Subtask 3 - Application Data Support.  The contractor shall load data to TCOSS, and provide support for secure customer access to, and
use of, data in TCOSS. General programming, analysis, and design tasks require no DoD 8570.01-M certification.  Code repository and system
administrative responsibilities (examples include backup, replication, security, migration to production) require DoD 8570.01-M certification
appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II, being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

6.5.3.1 The contractor shall load the monthly DITCO billing data and DFAS billing data.

6.5.3.2 The contractor shall provide ad-hoc reporting and data set extractions requested by customers, after coordination with the COR/ACOR.
The contractor shall identify the requesting customers and report about the kind, number, and frequency of data set extractions.

Deliverable:     Data set extractions report

6.5.3.3 The contractor shall maintain the TCOSS to DDOE financial approval interface.

6.5.3.4 The contractor shall resolve issues with provisioning responsibility assignment and message distribution.

6.5.3.5 The contractor shall identify and resolve data quality issues with received documents and data sets.

6.5.3.6 The contractor shall work with PM and COR/ACOR to resolve and improve data integrity issues between DISA and DITCO automation systems
and TCOSS.

6.5.3.7 The contractor shall manage document and graphical image data storages.

6.5.3.8 The contractor shall respond to changes in data sets and their formats for imported data obtained from sources outside of TCOSS in order
to modify the import application or transform the imported data set.
6.5.3.9 The contractor shall maintain the data set to cross reference Unit ID Codes (UIC) to Geographic Location Codes (GEOLOC) and DISA DITCO
city-state names.

6.5.4  Subtask 4 - Database and Data Administration.  The contractor shall maintain and administer database structures, coding, data content and
integrity, and the database management systems of TCOSS.  General programming, analysis, and design tasks require no DoD 8570.01-M
certification.  Code repository and system administrative responsibilities (examples include backup, replication, security, migration to
production) require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II, being Security+ or its equivalents at
Level II.

6.5.4.1 The contractor shall manage and maintain Microsoft SQL database servers.  Manage and maintain application databases, scripts, queries,
and other database management system elements hosted on Microsoft SQL database servers.

6.5.4.2 The contractor shall architect, design, and implement databases supporting automated applications.

6.5.4.3 The contractor shall manage and maintain data relations and integrity.

6.5.4.4 The contractor shall plan, backup, test, and restore the TCOSS database, including data, software, and associated support elements.

Deliverable: Database backup management plan

6.5.4.4.1  The contractor shall establish and perform database backup.  Perform database backup on a regular basis, no less than weekly.

6.5.4.4.2 The contractor shall restore database from backup. Restore the database from the backup, both partially and in its entirety, in
accordance with the database backup management plan.

6.5.4.4.3 The contractor shall maintain and update database backup procedures. Update the backup procedures when in accordance with DoD and AF
Directives, Instructions, and other official guidance, and the database backup management plan, and provide the COR/ACOR a copy of the backup
procedures with all updates for review and validation.  Report on equipment requirements.

6.5.4.4.4 The contractor shall regularly, test the capability of restoration procedures.  Analyze and report results of the test to the COR.

6.5.4.6 The contractor shall manage and maintain linked server connections from the Microsoft SQL server to the remote DDOE Oracle database
servers.

6.5.5  Subtask 5 - Customer Support.  The contractor shall provide support to customers of TCOSS.  While many customer support and training
activities do not require DoD 8570.01-M certification, certain system administrative responsibilities (examples include data system user account
setup and maintenance, and data set installation)  require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II,
being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

6.5.5.1 The contractor shall provide support for application users on local clients, remote clients, and Web users during normal office duty
hours.

6.5.5.2 The contractor shall provide TCOSS application support as well as network account management.

6.5.5.3 The contractor shall track and report requirements, trouble reports, and fix actions.

6.5.5.4 The contractor shall track and report contact and resolution rates.

6.5.5.5 The contractor shall perform trend analysis of problem reports to identify system problems. Include availability and reliability rates.

Deliverables:    Trend analysis report
            Solutions and timeline to correct problems

6.5.5.6 The contractor shall provide customer training in use of TCOSS.  Develop customer training utilizing Defense Connect Online (DCO).
Present descriptions of TCOSS use and operation as part of DISN Services class.

Deliverables:    Identify training tasks
            Training Plan
            Training modules in DCO

6.5.5.7 The contractor shall advise users in updating internal reference data directly from application data sets.

6.5.5.8 The contractor shall obtain updated data sets for application lookup reference data from DISA.

6.5.5.9 The contractor shall collect and record Change Requests from customers.  Follow procedures outlined in the TCOSS Change and Release
Management Guide.

6.5.5.10  The contractor shall conduct preliminary analysis of CCB-approved TCOSS change request.  Preliminary analysis will assess scope,
resources (material, time, funding, personnel), and feasibility.

Deliverable:     Analysis report

6.5.6 Subtask 6  Security and Information Assurance.  The contractor, in coordination with Government staff, shall be responsible for
applications and network security including maintaining certification and accreditation.  System administrative responsibilities (examples
include backup, replication, security, administration of development and production servers) require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to
Category IA Managerial (IAM) at Level II, being CISSP or its equivalents at Level II.  An IAM Level I certification is not acceptable.

6.5.6.1 The contractor shall perform all tasks related to network security and network processing accreditation.  Brief PM on progress
periodically.

6.5.6.2 The contractor shall prepare system accreditation and networthiness documentation packages, in accordance with applicable DoD and Air
Force instruction, to ensure TCOSS attains and maintains system and network accreditation and networthiness.

Deliverable: Entries in eMASS, EITDR, and documentation

6.5.6.3 The contractor shall comply promptly with DoD and AF directives including security bulletins and patches.

6.5.6.4 The contractor shall perform security testing and evaluation of software and network and correct identified deficiencies.

Deliverable:     Security test results report

6.5.6.5 The contractor shall provide support for the Air Force and DISA implementation of the DoD Information Assurance Certification and
Accreditation Process (DIACAP) and other certification and accreditation processes. Support may include, but not be limited to, modifications to
the database structure, creation of automatic electronic messaging or reports, and document creation.

6.5.6.6 The contractor shall provide Information Assurance management for software applications, and shall adhere strictly to instructions in
DODI 8500.2, Information Assurance (IA) Implementation, AFPD 33-2 Information Assurance and Air Force 33-200 Information Assurance (IA)
Management.

6.5.6.7 The contractor shall register software applications, and maintain security controls and other documentation. The contractor shall
document all security information in designated Air Force repositories, such as Enterprise Information Technology Data Repository (EITDR) or
Enterprise Mission Assurance Support Service (eMASS).

6.5.6.8 The contractor shall install security patches in accordance with AF instructions, policy and network tasking orders/directives.

6.5.6.9 The contractor shall complete weekly and annual Federal Information Security Management Act (FISMA) reports.

Deliverables:     FISMA reports

6.5.6.10 The contractor shall run scan using the current DISA-approved vulnerability scanning tool on all servers monthly in accordance with DoD
and AF directives.  Report findings to COR.  Resolve discrepancies and issues in accordance with DoD and AF directives.

Deliverables:    Findings and resolutions

6.5.6.11 The contractor shall maintain, update, and execute the TCOSS Vulnerability Management Plan.

6.5.6.12 The contractor shall validate vulnerability resolution and mitigations for TCOSS.

6.5.6.13 The contractor shall ensure that IA and IA enabled software, hardware, and firmware complies with appropriate security configuration
guidelines, policies, and procedures.

Deliverable:     Information Assurance Report

6.5.6.14 The contractor shall interpret patterns of non-compliance to determine their impact on levels of risk and/or overall effectiveness of
the IA program.

Deliverable:     Information Assurance Report

6.5.6.15 The contractor shall monitor and evaluate the effectiveness of the IA security procedures and safeguards to ensure they provide the
intended level of protection.

Deliverable:     Information Assurance Report

6.5.6.16 The contractor shall serve as the TCOSS Functional System Administrator (FSA).  The contractor shall comply with DOD and Air Force
directives, including self inspection program requirements for FSA duties.

6.5.7 Subtask 7 - Network Support.  The contractor shall administer TCOSS application and web servers, whether physical or virtual. System
administrative responsibilities (examples include backup, replication, security, administration of development and production servers) require
DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Managerial (IAM) at Level II, being CISSP or its equivalents at Level II.  An IAM Level I
certification is not acceptable.

6.5.7.1 The contractor shall administer and maintain data, file, Web, application, and other TCOSS servers running Windows and Microsoft IIS.

6.5.7.2 The contractor shall administer and maintain SQL database servers.

6.5.7.3 The contractor shall maintain hardware and software configuration management for servers and workstations in accordance with DOD and AF
policy and directives.

6.5.7.5 The contractor shall perform trend analysis of TCOSS application and performance over the network, using such data as uptime and
application responsiveness.

Deliverable: Analysis included in Monthly Status Review.

6.5.7.6 The contractor shall maintain system backups and ensure physical data protection.

6.5.7.7 The contractor, working with the COR/ACOR, shall develop and maintain the hardware and software technical refresh plan for TCOSS.

Deliverable:     Hardware and software tech refresh plan

6.5.7.8 The contractor shall review server event logs on all servers and back up; identify, report, and resolve any issues discovered.

Deliverable:     Report on any issues
            Plan and timeline to resolve issues

6.5.7.9 The contractor shall review backup logs and perform offsite cataloging and test restoral to ensure critical backup data sets are useable
and complete.

6.5.7.10 The contractor shall review Web logs at least weekly to ensure no issues exist.

Deliverable:     Report any problems

6.5.7.11 The contractor shall maintain TCOSS active directory, update users and group accounts.  Work with 375 Communications Group (Scott AFB)
to administer assigned TCP/IP addresses needed for TCOSS server and Contractor team workstation access.

6.5.7.12 The contractor shall install and maintain GFE workstation, server, and network hardware.  Install, maintain and support assigned
Contractor workstation, server and network hardware to include government-furnished workstations, TCOSS servers, and TCOSS-associated network
equipment.  Comply with Air Force directives, technical orders, and guidance to include establishment and maintenance of the Electrostatic
Discharge Program as it pertains to these duties.

6.5.7.13  The contractor shall install and maintain server configurations received as GFE, including the virtualized server environments.
Identify and resolve issues with those configurations as they arise.  Configuration improvements not involving addition of new hardware or
software should be documented and discussed with the COR for approval.

6.5.8 Subtask 8. TCOSS Management.  General programming, analysis, and design tasks require no DoD 8570.01-M certification.  Code repository and
system administrative responsibilities (examples include backup, replication, security, migration to production) require DoD 8570.01-M
certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II, being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

6.5.8.1 The contractor shall provide Program Management Reviews at least twice each year.

Deliverable:     Slides
            Minutes

6.5.8.2 Working with the COR/ACOR, the contractor shall update the TCOSS Change and Release Management Guide.

6.5.8.3 Working with the PM and COR, the contractor shall plan CCB meetings and prepare agenda.  Forward agenda to the PM for review and
approval.

Deliverable:     Agenda
            Slides
            Minutes

6.5.8.4 Working with the COR, the contractor shall update the TCOSS Configuration Management Plan as necessary.

6.5.8.5 Perform quarterly Disaster Recovery plan test.

Deliverable:      Briefing

6.5.8.6 For any and all software packages desired for addition to the suite of software used by the Sustainment or (if exercised) Optional
Development Teams for TCOSS, whether on workstations or servers, the contractor shall prepare requests to the CCB for approval.  No package,
regardless of origin or cost, may be used or added to the suite without permission of the PM and CCB.

6.5.9  Subtask 9 - Support of the TCOSS Development Team.  In the event that the Option for TCOSS Development is exercised one or more times,
provide that team or teams guidance to the current processes and tools.  The contractor shall provide support needed for access to resources
controlled by the Sustainment Team.  The sustainment team will administer the code repository, server systems, and network elements.  In the
event of unresolvable conflict, appeal the issue to the  COR.

6.6 Reserved.

6.7 Task 7 - Transition preparation for individuals and the contract.  All contractor team members shall perform this task.


6.7.1 Subtask 1  Provide continuity documentation.  The contractor shall provide for documentation that is composed, regularly updated, and
provided to the Government to ensure the continuity of task performance in the event of personnel turnover on the contract.  This documentation
shall also be made available to the successor contract staff member.  Such continuity folders should contain useful information for performing
tasks.  Examples include contact information for personnel (both Contractor and Government), systems access addresses, process descriptions,
useful tips, and useful documents not otherwise made available under the contract.

Deliverable:     Continuity folder

6.7.2 Subtask 2  Provide contract continuity documentation.  The contractor shall provide for a contract continuity documentation set composed,
regularly updated, and provided to the Government each year, three months prior to the end of the annual period of performance, for the purpose
of permitting uninterrupted continuation of the activities of the contract in the event of a transition to another Contractor or to execution by
Government employees.  The continuity documentation set shall include a primary document with the name, brief description, and storage location
of documents, program code, software tools, databases, and other items necessary to the contract tasks.  Documents delivered in the course of
performing other identified tasks need be only be referenced.

Deliverable:     Contract continuity document

6.8  Task 8 - Travel.  The contractor shall prepare for possible occasional short-duration travel.  Travel to other installation sites,
meetings, and conferences is occasionally required to support LHC mission requirements and inform customers.  Travel may be local (defined as
within 50 miles of the usual Contractor personnel work site [see paragraph 8, Place of Performance]) or long distance, including international.
Local travel costs shall not be at the expense of the Government.  The Contractor should plan on approximately 45 trips yearly of one to three
people each to sites around the globe, both inside and outside the United States.  All travel must be authorized by only the PM, COR or
Alternate COR, in advance of the travel.  The Contractor shall keep TDY travel requirements and costs to a minimum, leveraging existing Defense
Connect Online or VTC capabilities to the maximum extent possible.  The Contractors designated representative (PM, Site Lead, or similar) shall
be notified in advance when the PM or COR requires travel.  Authorization to travel shall be approved by the PM or COR by means of letter, E-
mail or form specifying: (1) The individual(s) to travel; (2) Purpose of the trip; (3) Location(s) and activities to be visited; and, (4)
Inclusive dates of the travel. Travel shall be charged to the Other Direct Cost (Travel) line of the contract in accordance with the directions
found in FAR 31.205-46 Travel Costs.


6.8.1 Subtask 1  Provide travel estimate, arrange travel, and provide trip report.  From time to time, Contractor personnel will be required to
travel in support of the LHC mission to educate, assist or provide Subject Matter Expertise for 38 CYRS/SCC or the LHC, as directed and approved
by PM or COR within the scope of this contract.  The Contractor shall provide an estimate of costs for each Contractor employee traveling
(including registration fees and other associated costs), as early as possible after the requirement is made known, but no later than one week
before travel.  Should travel be required within a week of departure date, a best-effort for the estimate delivery is acceptable.  Travel shall
be charged to the Other Direct Cost (Travel) line of the contract in accordance with the FAR 31.205-46 Travel Costs.  Where reimbursement of
travel is required from the LHC customer, contact information shall be provided to the PM, COR, and Long Haul financial personnel for Government
action.  No profit or fee will be paid for travel.  It is desired that subcontractor travel expenses, if any, be presented on the monthly
contract invoice to the same level of detail as those of the prime contractor, the better to track actual costs in relation to estimated costs.

Deliverables:    Travel estimate
            Trip report

6.9 Task 9 - Commercial Satellite Support under FCSA contract (formerly MSS and AF Teleport).  The contractor shall provide Commercial SATCOM
SME support, as enabled by the DISA FCSA contract.  This task does not require DoD 8570.01-M certification.   The authorized allotted FTE range
count for this task is two to three (2-3).

6.9.1 Subtask 1 - Coordinate circuit actions.  The contractor shall coordinate actions between AF customer and commercial provider with
activating, barring or deactivating mobile satellite circuits.

6.9.2 Subtask 2 - Manage mobile satellite database.  The contractor shall manage mobile satellite database records in TCOSS and AFEMS.

6.9.3 Subtask 3 - Provide customer support.  The contractor shall provide customer support to AF mobile satellite customers.

6.9.4 Subtask 4 - Review new or updated DoD, CJCS, and DISA directives and instructions.   The contractor shall determine how changes will
affect AF policy/governance; develop briefing and present to the government on how changes will impact AF mobile satellite policy.

6.9.5 Subtask 5 - Provide input to AF policy and governance.   The contractor shall provide policy development assistance to AF representatives
in determining the mobile satellite policy.

6.9.6 Subtask 6 -Transition mobile satellite assets/services from expiring DISA/DITCO contracts to new contracts.  The contractor shall
coordinate with MAJCOMs and units to transition mobile satellite hardware assets and services from expiring contracts to new contracts.

6.9.7 Subtask 7 - Manage annual Commercial SATCOM inventory.  The contractor shall manage Commercial SATCOM inventory and prepare annual usage
report.

Deliverable:     Usage report

6.9.8 Subtask 8 - Maintain list.  The contractor shall maintain list of MAJCOM mobile satellite managers.

6.9.9 Subtask 9 - Coordinate transfer of mobile assets.  The contractor shall coordinate transfer of mobile satellite assets between MAJCOMs,
FOAs, and DRUs.

6.9.10 Subtask 10 - Provide remote training.  The contractor shall provide remote training to mobile satellite managers on such actions as
activation and deactivation processes, use of the Satellite Authorization Request Form (SARF), discontinuing of services, and Satellite Database
requirements.

6.9.11 Subtask 11 - AF SME for Teleport and MSS.  As AF SME for Teleport and MSS, the contractor shall maintain thorough understanding of AF/DoD
policies and documents pertaining to the Teleport and MSS Programs, including the proceedings and decisions of the Commercial SATCOM/Gateway
Operations working group.

6.9.12 Subtask 12 - Work with AF customers and DISA.  The contractor shall work with AF customers and the DISA Teleport Program Office to
resolve teleport issues and advance AF requirements.

6.9.13 Subtask 13 - User requirements.  The contractor shall gather and identify all AF Teleport user requirements.

6.9.14 Subtask 14 - Oversee the AF portion of the DoD teleport program.  The contractor shall provide oversight of AF activity in the Teleport
program.

6.9.15 Subtask 15 -  Review Engineering Change Requests.  The contractor shall review Engineering Change Requests for Air Force impacts.
Coordinate impacts that will affect the AF with the mobile satellite/teleport ACOR.

6.10  (Optional)  Task 10 - TCOSS Systems Development.  The contractor shall perform all software development functions to add new capabilities
to TCOSS.  All such development processes and new capabilities must comply with DoD, Joint, AF, DISA, MAJCOM, and Scott AFB standards for
interoperability, software lifecycle, security, and customer support Directives, Instructions, Memoranda, and other official guidance.
Developers will perform all subtasks of Task 5 TCOSS: Maintenance, Security, and Customer Support (paragraph 6.5) appropriate to adding
capabilities to the system, and will cooperate with the sustainment team in all aspects.  New capabilities will be developed and added only
after approval by PM in Configuration Control Board (CCB) and provision of funds.    Conflicts between development and sustainment teams will be
elevated to the ACOR or COR for resolution.  General programming, analysis, and design tasks require no DoD 8570.01-M certification.  Code
repository and system administrative responsibilities (examples include backup, replication, security, migration to production) require DoD
8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II, being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.  The authorized
allotted FTE range count for this task is zero to six (0-6).


6.10.1  Subtask 1- Design and Documentation.  Following CCB approval of preliminary analysis of proposal, the contractor shall perform full
analysis of the proposed work, to include all code, database structures, documentation, and hardware adaptations or additions.  Estimate
resources required, to include time, levels of expertise, and schedule (at minimum).  Documentation must supplement existing TCOSS documentation
(for example, documents for the user and system) in compatible style and format without forcing extensive rewriting of existing documentation.
Access to approved documentation must be open to all TCOSS team members, Long Haul Communication management (COR, ACORs, PM), and
representatives of the entity which requested the new capability.  Initial documentation must be updated throughout the development process and
completed at the end of development.

Deliverables:    Documentation of new capabilitys purpose, structure, design, and use
            Estimate of development resources required

6.10.2  Subtask 2 - Code.  The contractor shall provide application code and data structures which implement the desired capability.  Code and
structures may be incorporated into existing routines and structures or be separate new elements, as appropriate.

Deliverable:     Code and data structures

6.10.3  Subtask 3  Create development metrics.  Beginning with each full estimate for a given task as constructed in subtask 1, the contractor
shall track actual resources used, and provide final report of metrics, comparing the estimate to the actual performance.

Deliverable:     Metric report

6.10.4  Subtask 4 - Processes.  The contractor development team shall  follow established administrative processes for system security, code
protection, migration, and implementation.  Suggestions for improvements may be offered, but revisions shall be made only with agreement of the
sustainment team and Air Force COR, and shall not deviate from official standards and guidance.  The contractor sustainment team shall
administer the code repository, server systems, and network elements.

6.10.5  Subtask 5 - TCOSS Maintenance, Security, and Customer Support.  The contractor development team shall perform all subtasks of Task 5
TCOSS: Maintenance, Security, and Customer Support (paragraph 6.5) appropriate to adding capabilities to the system, and will cooperate with
the sustainment team in all aspects.

6.10.6  Subtask 6 - Continuity.  The contractor development team shall create and maintain continuity documentation as described in Task 7
(paragraph 6.7) regardless of the projected duration of the development team.

6.10.7  Subtask 7 - Travel.  The contractor development team shall perform Task 8 (paragraph 6.8).  However, travel by development team members
will be only that required to support development tasks under this Optional Task.  An example of such required travel may be to inform the user
funding and requiring a given development of progress in the task.  All travel must be approved by the PM or COR.

6.11 (Optional)  Task 11- Commercial Satellite Management Office (CSMO).  (NOTE: This task is an option which may be invoked in the event the
task is assigned to 38 CYRS/SCC.  )  Perform support of Air Force satellite communication services (described in Task 9, paragraph 6.9, and this
Task 11, paragraph 6.11)  in a consolidated group, supporting MSS, FSS, and Air Force Teleport satellite services.  The distinguishing
difference here is the addition of tasks supporting the Satellite Communications element formerly known as FSS.  This task does not require DoD
8570.01-M certification.  The authorized allotted FTE range count for this task is three to six (3-6), inclusive of those performing Task 9.

6.11.1 Subtask 1 - Performance of Task 11.  The contractor shall perform all tasks of Task 9 - Commercial Satellite Support under FCSA contract
(formerly MSS and AF Teleport) (paragraph 6.9) as part of this task.

6.11.2 Subtask 2 - Joint Staff Action package (JSAP) tracking.  The contractor shall identify and track all AF commercial satellite
communications (COMSATCOM) hardware and leased services per the JSAP.

6.11.3 Subtask 3 - Produce usage report.  The contractor shall produce the annual usage report, providing it to the Government CSMO lead.

Deliverable:     Annual usage report

6.11.4 Subtask 4  Monitor subscription usage.  The contractor shall monitor AF COMSATCOM subscription usage for billing anomalies through the
service providers.  Provide recommendations to the field for COMSATCOM solutions.

6.11.5 Subtask 5  Represent AF for commercial satellite communications.  The contractor shall represent AF for COMSATCOM at the Net-Centric 
Capabilities Portfolio Management (NC-CPM). Represent AF to coordinate policy and planning guidance at the Joint level to achieve cost-effective
interoperable COMSATCOM infrastructure solutions across the DoD.

6.11.6 Subtask6  Coordinate CIPS requirement process for COMSATCOM capabilities.  The contractor shall coordinate the CIPS requirements process
for AF COMSATCOM capabilities.  DODI 8100.04 Unified Capabilities (UC) defines COMSATCOM as UC transport. Serve as SME and provide recommended
solutions for acquisition of COMSATCOM hardware and services through the AF requirements process.

6.11.7 Subtask 7  Participate in testing of COMSATCOM products and services.  The contractor shall work with JITC, MAJCOMs/FOAs/DRUs to
participate in operational testing, compatibility, and interoperability testing and evaluation of COMSATCOM products and services.

6.11.8 Subtask 8  Assist planning of AF COMSATCOM funding.  In coordination with MAJCOMs/FOAs/DRUs, the contractor shall aid in planning future
funding in support of their AF COMSATCOM.

6.11.9 Subtask 9  Coordinate AF COMSATCOM training needs identification.  The contractor shall coordinate with AETC and AF Career Field
Managers to ensure AF COMSATCOM training needs are identified.

6.11.10 Subtask 10  Review waiver requests.  The contractor shall review MAJCOM/DRU/FOA requested waivers to procure and use non-standard AF
COMSATCOM systems and/or services and assist 38 CYRS/SCC in coordinating through AFSPC to SAF/A6 for approval.

6.11.11 Subtask 11  Review database record structure.  The contractor shall review the data structures and code for MSS and Teleport records in
TCOSS to assess suitability for use with FSS records.  Identify courses of action  options for  incorporating Air Force FSS records, dating from
before the award of the FCSA contract, into TCOSS, and including establishment of one or more interfaces into an existing FSS tracking database.
 Report results of this exploration to the COR.

6.12 (Optional) Task 12 - FaCIT Development, Sustainment, and Customer Support.  At Maxwell AFB-Gunter Annex, all FaCIT lifecycle processes
(examples include development, sustainment, testing, Information Assurance, customer support, documentation, and management processes) shall be
performed by the contractor in accordance with the Systems Engineering Process (SEP) and relevant Air Force and DoD regulations and standards.
Please note that, because of the local development environment in use, DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at
Level II, being Security+ or its equivalent at level II is required for all team personnel.  The authorized allotted FTE range count for this
task is four to seven (4-7).

6.12.1 Subtask 1  Development and sustainment.  The contractor shall perform software development and sustainment for the FaCIT
application/system.  General programming, analysis, and design tasks as well as code repository and system administrative responsibilities
(examples include backup, replication, security, migration to production) require certification to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II,
being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

6.12.1.1 The contractor shall perform software development and maintenance in accordance with the Systems Engineering Process (SEP) for FaCIT
and its configuration management processes.

6.12.1.2  The contractor shall document the baseline establishment.  Ensure all baselined CIs are in a centralized Government-controlled area
(i.e. Configuration Management Library, a configuration management tool).

6.12.1.3 The contractor shall maintain and control access to artifacts in the Configuration Management Library.

6.12.1.4 The contractor shall audit the Configuration Item (CI) performance.  Audit the CI against its approved configuration documentation to
verify the customer's functional requirements are incorporated.

6.12.1.5  The contractor shall regularly compare the production software to the software in the project's Configuration Management Library.
Report and correct discrepancies.

6.12.1.6 The contractor shall develop the Project Configuration Management Plan (CMP).  Review, coordinate, and ensure approval of the Project
CMP.

Deliverable:     Configuration Management Plan

6.12.1.7 The contractor shall identify the structure of work products so the Configuration Items for a project may be controlled by establishing
designated configuration baselines.

6.12.1.8 The contractor shall manage the change process for the baseline configuration and track those changes to ensure the configuration of
the system work products is known at all times.

Deliverable:     Memo to FaCIT PM

6.12.1.9 The contractor shall facilitate the Configuration Control Board (CCB).

6.12.1.9.1 The contractor shall prepare, coordinate and maintain an official membership appointment letter.

6.12.1.9.2 The contractor shall prepare and distribute the Configuration Control Board agenda.

6.12.1.9.3 The contractor shall annotate Configuration Control Board actions in the minutes.

6.12.1.9.4 The contractor shall obtain approval of the Configuration Control Directive.

6.12.1.9.5 The contractor shall prepare and distribute CCB minutes and Action Item (AIs) assignments.

Deliverables:     CCB meeting minutes

6.12.1.10 The contractor shall provide project and technical support.

6.12.1.10.1 The contractor shall assist in development of cost data in support of the program.

6.12.1.10.2 The contractor shall assist with technical evaluations for procurement actions.

6.12.1.10.3 The contractor shall attend meetings and conferences in person or via telecomm.

6.12.1.10.4 The contractor shall monitor timelines for all activities such as document reviews.

6.12.1.11 The contractor shall provide task management support.

6.12.1.11.1 The contractor shall serve as on-site project lead for the contract.

6.12.1.11.2 The contractor shall serve as the single point of contact between government and Contractor personnel.

6.12.1.11.3 The contractor shall be responsible for organizing, directing, and coordinating work assignments.

6.12.1.11.4 The contractor shall be responsible for organizing resources to support many concurrent activities and manages the execution of
multiple concurrent activities.

6.12.1.12 The contractor shall provide test and evaluation support.

6.12.1.12.1 The contractor shall be responsible for testing all software prior to approving for implementing on the operational system as
practical with any appropriate action taken after results are finalized.

6.12.1.12.2 The contractor shall prepare any documentation to accompany release of new software required by site personnel.

6.12.1.13 The contractor shall provide functional analyst support by applying a thorough knowledge of the functional requirements and
specifications.

6.12.1.13.1 As lead functional analyst, the contractor shall perform as the project test leader.

6.12.1.13.2 The contractor shall be responsible for analyzing and refining customer requirements.

6.12.1.13.3 The contractor shall provide authoritative guidance on applicable functional standards and certify whether the software application
satisfies requirements.

6.12.1.14 The contractor shall provide technical requirements analyst support.

6.12.1.14.1 The contractor shall facilitate and model the business process and information flow analysis for the project.

6.12.1.14.2 The contractor shall implement and lead technical approaches to elicit requirements, represent requirements in text diagrams,
organize requirements and their attributes in a requirements management system, and validate the requirements.

6.12.1.14.3 The contractor shall perform analyses on user needs and translates these needs into application delivery requirements and designs.

6.12.1.14.4 The contractor shall ensure requested user needs do not conflict with existing documented requirements.

6.12.1.14.5 The contractor shall ensure each technical specification is traceable to a documented need.

6.12.1.14.6 The contractor shall examine and evaluate alternative means of satisfying user requirements and suggests technically feasible
approaches.

6.12.1.14.7 The contractor shall modify and adapt application logic to unique or specialized requirements.

6.12.1.14.8 The contractor shall make recommendations on project interrelationships that must be considered in producing the output desired.

6.12.1.15.9      The contractor shall analyze complex acceptance test failures; recommends solution and documents the solution and risk to
system for management decision.

6.12.1.15 The contractor shall provide lead development and design support.

6.12.1.15.1 The contractor shall be responsible for designing the technical solution and all the documents that supports it.

6.12.1.15.2 The contractor shall be responsible for implementing and testing the design.

6.12.1.15.3 The contractor shall determine if the application meets the design specifications and responsible for being the development test
representative.

6.12.1.16 The contractor shall ensure all code is Year 2000 compliant.

6.12.2 Subtask 2 - Customer Support.  The contractor shall provide user support and problem resolution for the FaCIT system.  While many
helpdesk and training activities do not require DoD 8570.01-M certification, certain system administrative responsibilities (examples include
data system user account setup and maintenance, and data set installation)  require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA
Technical (IAT) at Level II, being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.

6.12.2.1 The contractor shall provide customer support to FaCIT application users.

6.12.2.2 The contractor shall provide assistance to site personnel to resolve open issues.

6.12.2.2.1 The contractor shall open trouble tickets in Remedy to track functional and user interface problems with the FaCIT application.  Non-
emergency trouble tickets shall be given a response within one business day.  Emergency trouble tickets shall be given a response within one
hour of receipt.  If any problem complaint is received after business hours, respond the next business day.

6.12.2.2.2 The contractor shall conduct a functional analysis to verify that the trouble is an actual FaCIT problem and not a user or computer
system error.

6.12.2.2.3 The contractor shall document all fix actions with after-action reports or document in the trouble ticket.

6.12.2.3 The contractor shall track requirements, trouble reports, and fix actions.

6.12.2.4 The contractor shall provide user contact and complaint resolution rates.

6.12.2.5 The contractor shall develop and/or maintain customer application training utilizing Defense Connect Online (DCO).

Deliverables:    Identify training tasks
            Build training modules in DCO

6.12.3 Subtask 3 - Security and Information Assurance.  The contractor, in coordination with Government staff, shall be responsible for
applications and network security including maintaining certification and accreditation.  System administrative responsibilities (examples
include backup, replication, security, administration of development and production servers) require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to
Category IA Managerial (IAM) at Level II, being CISSP or its equivalents at Level II.  An IAM Level I certification is not acceptable.

6.12.3.1  The contractor shall perform all tasks related to network security and network processing accreditation.  Brief PM, FaCIT PM, and
COR/ACOR on progress periodically.

6.12.3.2 The contractor shall prepare system accreditation documentation packages.

6.12.3.3 The contractor shall comply with DoD and AF directives including security bulletins and patches.

6.12.3.4 The contractor shall perform security testing and evaluation of network.

6.12.3.5 The contractor shall research, review, and implement service level network security standards and policies.

6.12.3.6 The contractor shall provide support for the Air Force and DISA implementation of the DoD Information Assurance Certification and
Accreditation Process (DIACAP) and other certification and accreditation processes.  Support may include, but not be limited to, modifications
to the database structure, creation of automatic electronic messaging or reports, and document creation.

6.12.3.7 The contractor shall provide Information Assurance management for software applications. Apply strict adherence to instructions in DODI
8500.2 Information Assurance (IA) Implementation, AFPD 33-2 Information Assurance and Air Force 33-200 Information Assurance (IA) Management.
6.12.3.8 The contractor shall coordinate security testing with independent testing agency ensuring the software application meets security
standards for inclusion on the AF Evaluated/Approved Products List.  For FaCIT version 7.0 and all following versions, meet the DIACAP security
standards of full information system Certification and Accreditation before fielding.

6.12.3.9 The contractor shall register software application, maintain security controls and other documentation, in such designated Air Force
repositories as Enterprise Information Technology Data Repository (EITDR) and Enterprise Mission Assurance Support Service (eMASS).

6.12.3.10 The contractor shall be responsible for maintaining situational awareness and initiating actions to improve or restore Information
Assurance.

6.12.3.11 The contractor shall be responsible for conducting annual security reviews of all Information Assurance controls and a test of
selected Information Assurance controls.

6.12.4 Subtask 4  Technology Integration and Software Testing.  The contractor shall be responsible for FaCIT testing, for providing migration
documentation, and shall identify new software for potential use in supporting FaCIT.  General programming, analysis, design and unit testing
tasks as well as code repository and system administrative responsibilities (examples include backup, replication, security, application
migration to production) under the FaCIT environment require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Technical (IAT) at Level II,
being Security+ or its equivalents at Level II.  Responsibilities of more extensive software integration testing, system testing, and system
migration to production require DoD 8570.01-M certification appropriate to Category IA Managerial  (IAM) at Level II, being CISSP or its
equivalents at Level II.  An IAM Level I certification is not acceptable.

6.12.4.1 The contractor shall be responsible for testing all software prior to approving for implementing on the operational network.

6.12.4.2 The contractor shall prepare and provide documentation supporting software testing and migration under the SEP.  Prepare additional
guidance for site personnel for use in migration and installation of FaCIT.

6.12.4.3 The contractor shall be responsible for identifying and recommending possible new software in support of the FaCIT architecture.

Deliverables:    Recommendation and impact

6.13 (Option) Task 13 - Air Force Forward Operating Agencies (FOA) and Direct Reporting Units (DRU). If the responsibility is given 38 CYRS/SCC,
the requirement of providing circuit management support for Air Force FOAs and DRUs will be added to the MAJCOM Circuit Management Office (CMO)
and the AF will fund and exercise this optional Task.  The contractor shall provide personnel to expand the CMO team to support these additional
Air Force units.  There shall be no distinction in the type and quality of support under this contract between that provided for AF MAJCOM, AF
MAJCOM subordinate units, and Combatant Command units on AF bases, and that provided for the Air Force FOAs and DRUs.  The contractor shall
perform Task 2 (paragraph 6.2) and Task 3 (paragraph 6.3) specifically, along with other common tasks.  The authorized allotted FTE range count
for this task is zero to three (0-3).
